      "body": "It is possible to specify custom certificate paths or path patterns for action `keychain add-certificates` via CLI option `--certificate`. As this option accepts either path literals, or a glob patterns to match certificates, then relative reference `.` to current directory should also be an acceptable input. This however results in an error when globbing matches:\r\n\r\n```python\r\n>>> list(Path().glob('.'))\r\nTraceback (most recent call last):\r\n  File \"/Users/priit/development/nevercode/cli-tools/.venv/lib/python3.12/site-packages/IPython/core/interactiveshell.py\", line 3553, in run_code\r\n    exec(code_obj, self.user_global_ns, self.user_ns)\r\n  File \"<ipython-input-23-b1f87bcdf599>\", line 1, in <cell line: 0>\r\n    list(Path().glob('.'))\r\n  File \"/Users/priit/.pyenv/versions/3.12.0/lib/python3.12/pathlib.py\", line 1094, in glob\r\n    selector = _make_selector(tuple(pattern_parts), self._flavour, case_sensitive)\r\n               ^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^\r\n  File \"/Users/priit/.pyenv/versions/3.12.0/lib/python3.12/pathlib.py\", line 83, in _make_selector\r\n    pat = pattern_parts[0]\r\n          ~~~~~~~~~~~~~^^^\r\nIndexError: tuple index out of range\r\n```\r\n\r\nTo overcome that limitation, just resolve the relative path pattern before attempting glob search. Then the path becomes absolute which can be safely globbed.\r\n\r\n**Updated actions:**\r\n- `keychain add-certificates`",

      "body": "Not sure if this is the best approach to fix the issue, but currently we [do not seem to be sending analytics reports for mac since March](https://iterativeai.slack.com/archives/CB41NAL8H/p1697464559356029?thread_ts=1697200360.717249&cid=CB41NAL8H). I have tested and found that it seems to be some combination of forking and the `_popen` method used. Analytics get sent successfully if I either:\r\n1. Drop all the forking logic, OR\r\n2. Call `main` like it does for linux.\r\n\r\nHere I dropped all the forking and conditions here and just use `_popen` directly. This successfully sends reports for me, and I'm not sure why we need forking here since it should happen in a separate, non-blocking process when using `_popen` (and dropping `.communicate()`). \r\n\r\nNot sure if I miss some context for why forking or other logic is needed (I took a look back at https://github.com/iterative/dvc/issues/4294 and https://github.com/iterative/dvc/pull/4262 but wasn't clear why this is all needed).",

\r\n\r\n```bash\r\n#!/bin/bash\r\n\r\nFOLDER=\"ecosystem/resources/members/*\"\r\ndeclare -a TER_VERSIONS=( \\\r\n  \"0.25.0\" \"0.24.0\" \"0.23.2\" \"0.23.1\" \"0.23.0\" \"0.23.0rc1\" \"0.22.4\" \"0.43.0\" \"0.41.1\" \"0.41.0\" \"0.40.0\" \"0.40.0\" \"0.39.5\" \"0.39.4\" \"0.39.2\" \"0.39.0\" \\\r\n  \"0.38.0\" \"0.37.1\" \"0.37.0\" \"0.36.2\" \"0.36.1\" \"0.36.0\" \"0.34.1\" \"0.32.1\" \"0.27.0\" \\\r\n)\r\n\r\nsearch_pac=\"terra_version\"\r\nreplace_pac=\"qiskit_version\"\r\n\r\nfor index in \"${!TER_VERSIONS[@]}\"\r\ndo\r\n  search_ver=\"${TER_VERSIONS[$index]}\"\r\n  replace_ver=\"${QIS_VERSIONS[$index]}\"\r\n\r\n  for file in ${FOLDER}\r\n  do\r\n    find \"${file}\" -type f -exec sed -i '' -e \"s,${search_ver},${replace_ver},g\" {} \\;\r\n    find \"${file}\" -type f -exec sed -i '' -e \"s,${search_pac},${replace_pac},g\" {} \\;\r\n    echo \"search: $search_ver - replace: $replace_ver\"\r\n\r\n  done\r\ndone\r\n```\r\n\r\n---\r\nCloses #486   ",

      "body": "*Issue #, if available:*\r\n\r\n*Description of changes:*\r\n\r\n- [x] TODO: Benchmark\r\n\r\nFixes infer_limit being incorrectly calculated when bagging\r\n\r\nThe fix involves using the post-refit (expected) infer time of models in all scenarios involving refit full and selecting the best model when `infer_limit` is specified.\r\n\r\nWith this fix, infer_limit should work as intended in all scenarios. For users who were already using `infer_limit` combined with bagging, it is recommended to lower the `infer_limit` value by a factor of 10 to maintain similar inference speed.\r\n\r\nSpecifically, the inference time values used were incorrect when 1. choosing the best model, and 2. choosing the best model during refit full with bagging enabled.\r\n\r\nIf a bagged model had 8 folds, it would use the infer time of all 8 fold models, rather than the expected _FULL refit model.\r\nThis led to scenarios where the models would satisfy the infer limit when refit, but were filtered out of consideration due to their non-refit infer times being used at the time of filtering.\r\n\r\nThis problem got worse with repeated bagging, leading to an up to 160x difference in infer time compared to expectation.\r\n\r\nWhen this problem occurs, it can lead to an exception in two ways:\r\n\r\nException 1: Occurs when the `model_best` changes when considering the `infer_limit`, and that changed model does not exist in refit because it was not the model that was refit.\r\n```\r\nTraceback (most recent call last):\r\n  File \"/bench/frameworks/shared/callee.py\", line 75, in call_run\r\n    result = run_fn(ds, config)\r\n  File \"/bench/frameworks/AutoGluon/exec.py\", line 73, in run\r\n    predictor = TabularPredictor(\r\n  File \"/bench/frameworks/AutoGluon/venv/lib/python3.9/site-packages/autogluon/core/utils/decorators.py\", line 30, in _call\r\n    return f(*gargs, **gkwargs)\r\n  File \"/bench/frameworks/AutoGluon/venv/lib/python3.9/site-packages/autogluon/tabular/predictor/predictor.py\", line 959, in fit\r\n    self._post_fit(\r\n  File \"/bench/frameworks/AutoGluon/venv/lib/python3.9/site-packages/autogluon/tabular/predictor/predictor.py\", line 1014, in _post_fit\r\n    self._trainer.calibrate_model()\r\n  File \"/bench/frameworks/AutoGluon/venv/lib/python3.9/site-packages/autogluon/core/trainer/abstract_trainer.py\", line 3041, in calibrate_model\r\n    y_val_probs = self.get_model_oof(model_name_og)\r\n  File \"/bench/frameworks/AutoGluon/venv/lib/python3.9/site-packages/autogluon/core/trainer/abstract_trainer.py\", line 967, in get_model_oof\r\n    model_type = self.get_model_attribute(model=model, attribute='type')\r\n  File \"/bench/frameworks/AutoGluon/venv/lib/python3.9/site-packages/autogluon/core/trainer/abstract_trainer.py\", line 2347, in get_model_attribute\r\n    model = model.name\r\nAttributeError: 'NoneType' object has no attribute 'name'\r\n```\r\n\r\nException 2: Occurs when the incorrect larger infer time values lead to 0 models satisfying the infer limit.\r\n```\r\nAssertionError: Trainer has no fit models that can infer while satisfying the constraints: (infer_limit=9.992981433868409e-05, allow_full=True).\r\n```\r\n\r\nBy submitting this pull request, I confirm that you can use, modify, copy, and redistribute this contribution, under the terms of your choice.\r\n",

      "body": "*Issue #, if available:*\r\n\r\n*Description of changes:*\r\n- Fix edge-case crash in `.refit_full('best')` when \"best\" differs between trainer and predictor (for example, when `WeightedEnsemble` only has 1 base model, and when predictor was fit with `_save_bag_folds=False`. Now the `\"best\"` model refit will be the predictor's \"best\" model to avoid an exception during `.predict(data)`\r\n- Fix edge-case crash when `.fit(..., _save_bag_folds=False, calibrate=True, refit_full=False)` where no models can infer and calibration is called, resulting in an exception. Now models that can't infer can be calibrated, which after refit_full results in calibrated refit models.\r\n\r\nBy submitting this pull request, I confirm that you can use, modify, copy, and redistribute this contribution, under the terms of your choice.\r\n",

error-status of the next or previous port\r\n2.\tâ€œsfputil show error-status -hw -p <port>â€ doesnâ€™t display error-status\r\n3. platform_tests/sfp/test_sfputil.py::test_check_sfputil_error_status sonic-mgmt testcase fails for some platforms\r\n\r\nIssue details with an example of sfp.index being 1 based while physical_port being 0 based:\r\nThe sfp.index https://github.com/sonic-net/sonic-utilities/blob/7435b1ca539382e644f29d424c551f6258fd2920/sfputil/main.py#L904 is 1 based whereas the physical port numbering is 0 based (retried from port_config.ini file).\r\nHence, for Ethernet0 (sfp.index = 1), there is no key-value defined in output_dict (dictionary of <sfp.index>:<error_status>) for physical_port = 0.\r\nhttps://github.com/sonic-net/sonic-utilities/blob/7435b1ca539382e644f29d424c551f6258fd2920/sfputil/main.py#L940\r\n\r\n#### How I did it\r\nI am now directly calling get_error_description using sfp object to retrieve the error description. This removes the dependency with sfp.index to retrieve error description for a port.\r\n\r\n#### How to verify it\r\nRan platform_tests/sfp/test_sfputil.py::test_check_sfputil_error_status sonic-mgmt testcase and ensured it passes successfully.\r\n\r\n#### Previous command output (if the output of a command-line utility has changed)\r\nNo change in CLI o/p.       "body": "## Overview\r\nThere were a couple of bugs and design changes that were made after testing emulations and the `auth` and `creds` commands.\r\n\r\n#### Issue: Sessions not available after credential storage from within emulations\r\nWhen running an emulation, credentials were available in the credential store, but an active session is needed to start a service client. However, `authenticate` in `auth.py` was a `Command` method and thus not available from emulations. To solve this, a static method was added that will take credentials and authenticate as normal, returning a session that can be used in the emulation.\r\n\r\nBelow is an example, where `default` contains service account credentials in the store. We pass it to `get_auth_session` and it returns an actual session.\r\n\r\n```python \r\nclass Emulation(BaseEmulation):\r\n\r\n    parser = BaseEmulation.load_parser(description='Account Manipulation: Additional Cloud Roles')\r\n    parser.add_argument('--username', required=True, help='Username to add the role to')\r\n    parser.add_argument('--roles', required=True, help='Roles to add')\r\n\r\n    techniques = ['T1098.003']\r\n\r\n    def __init__(self, **kwargs) -> None:\r\n        super().__init__(**kwargs)\r\n        self.session = AuthCommand.get_auth_session(creds=self.obj.cred_store.store['default'].creds.to_dict(), type='service')\r\n        self.service = build('drive', 'v3', credentials=self.session)\r\n\r\n    def execute(self) -> None:\r\n        self.elogger.info(self.exec_str(self.parser.description))\r\n```\r\n\r\n#### `auth` command does not store the sessions, only the credentials by default in the credential store.\r\nIf users would prefer to store both the credentials and session after authentication, they can now use `--store NAME` and it will store those credentials and session in the credential store. This allows us to authenticate -> store credentials -> store session -> access in emulations.\r\n\r\n#### `PosixPath` stored in credential store\r\nOriginally, if `auth` was used to authenticate, the path of the credentials was being stored as `creds` in the credential store. This has been adjusted to determine if it is a `Path` and if so, load it `from_file` with `OAuthCreds` or `ServiceAccountCreds` and save it as the actual JSON object.\r\n",

      "body": "After the update to 3.8.0 we notices that our more advanced sql.query's where not working anymore.\r\nWe found that after version 2.0 of SQLAlchemy the method for passing string queries using the `conn.execute(query)` was  removed (https://docs.sqlalchemy.org/en/20/core/connections.html#sqlalchemy.engine.Connection.execute):\r\n\r\n> Changed in version 2.0: The [Connection.execution_options()](https://docs.sqlalchemy.org/en/20/core/connections.html#sqlalchemy.engine.Connection.execution_options) method, in contrast to other objects with this method, modifies the connection in-place without creating copy of it.\r\n\r\nSo we implemented the exec_driver_sql function which does support passing queries in string format.\r\nWe also noticed that the deriving the keys from a tuple was not stable for our queries. So we implemented the internal `_asdict()` function into the loop to auto-convert the tuples to a parsable dict-type.",

      "body": "# Description\r\n\r\nThis is a simple fix to make the celery worker kick off under the `exec` command. This ensures that the PID is transferred to the celery worker, so the `SIGTERM` signal is actually received. It was tested and observed that the `SIGTERM` does not pass through celery without calling with `exec`.\r\n\r\nThis does not fix the connection timeout but should prevent the task from terminating before completion.\r\n\r\n#1251 \r\n\r\n## Type of change\r\n\r\nPlease delete options that are not relevant.\r\n\r\n- [x] Bug fix (non-breaking change which fixes an issue)\r\n- [x] New feature (non-breaking change which adds functionality)\r\n\r\n## How Has This Been Tested?\r\n\r\nThis was [deployed](https://github.com/department-of-veterans-affairs/notification-api/actions/runs/5007818954) to dev. It was observed that the hooks were being called, as shown in our logs (documented in #1251). Forced redeploy showed that the workers were receiving `SIGTERM` as expected. Prior to this change the hooks were not being called. \r\n\r\n17:16:50 the service was force redeployed\r\n17:18:32 the `SIGTERM` was processed\r\n17:18:32 the workers were shut down because they had no tasks running\r\n\r\n## Checklist\r\n- [x] My code follows the style guidelines of this project\r\n- [x] I have performed a self-review of my own code\r\n- [x] I have commented my code, particularly in hard-to-understand areas\r\n- [x] My changes generate no new warnings\r\n- [x] New and existing unit tests pass locally with my changes\r\n",

Use closing keywords when appropriate -->\r\nResolves #2931 \r\nResolves #2930\r\n\r\n## Summary\r\n\r\nSome fields are not public using the API. This PR removes these fields based on stack schema versions (min and max) so that the fields aren't used when trying to upload the rule to a different stack version (see the issue for more details).\r\n\r\n- Uses a stack version (user provided or pulled from rule or default to 8.3.0) to remove non public fields\r\n- Adds a new `strip_non_public_fields` method to __init__ and NON_PUBLIC_FIELDS variable in definitions\r\n- Strips the fields prior to uploading.\r\n- Rewrites `downgrade_contents_from_rule` to downgrade and validate the `to_dict` version of the rule, then builds and new TOMLRuleContents object to obtain a `to_api_format` payload prior to uploading.\r\n\r\n\r\n### Testing\r\n\r\n<details><summary>Testing on Old Branches</summary>\r\n<p>\r\n\r\nThe '\r\n             'This is a [New '\r\n             'Terms](https://www.elastic.co/guide/en/security/master/rules-ui-create.html#create-new-terms-rule) '\r\n             'rule indicating this is the first time a specific user '\r\n             'identity has successfuly retrieved a secret value from '\r\n             'Secrets Manager.\\n'\r\n             '\\n'\r\n             '#### Possible investigation steps\\n'\r\n             '\\n'\r\n             '- Identify the account and its role in the environment, and '\r\n             'inspect the related policy.\\n'\r\n             '- Identify the applications that should use this account.\\n'\r\n             '- Investigate other alerts associated with the user account '\r\n             'during the past 48 hours.\\n'\r\n             '- Investigate abnormal values in the `user_agent.original` '\r\n             'field by comparing them with the intended and authorized '\r\n             'usage and historical data.
